the

of
the

members
of

<p>In
their
native
United
Kingdom
during
1962–1970,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>
released
12
<a
href="/wiki/Studio_album?qsrc=3044"
title="Studio
album">studio
albums</a>,
13
<a
href="/wiki/Extended_play?qsrc=3044"
title="Extended
play">EPs</a>,
and
22
<a
href="/wiki/Single_(music)?qsrc=3044"
title="Single
(music)">singles</a>.
However,
the
band's
international
<a
href="/wiki/Discography?qsrc=3044"
title="Discography">discography</a>
is
complicated,
due
to
different
versions
of
their
albums
sometimes
being
released
in
other
countries,
particularly
during
their
early
years
on
<a
href="/wiki/Capitol_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Capitol
Records">Capitol
Records</a>
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles%27_American_releases?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles'
American
releases">in
the
United
States</a>.
The
Beatles'
discography
was
originally
released
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Gramophone_record?qsrc=3044"
title="Gramophone
record">vinyl</a>
format,
with
full-length
<a
href="/wiki/LP_record?qsrc=3044"
title="LP
record">long
plays</a>
(LPs),
shorter
EPs,
and
singles
(SPs).
Over
the
years,
the
collection
has
also
been
released
on
<a
href="/wiki/Compact_Cassette?qsrc=3044"
title="Compact
Cassette">cassette</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/8-track_tape?qsrc=3044"
title="8-track
tape">8-track</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Compact_Disc?qsrc=3044"
title="Compact
Disc">compact
disc</a>
(CD),
and
on
a
<a
href="/wiki/USB_flash_drive?qsrc=3044"
title="USB
flash
drive">USB
flash
drive</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/MP3?qsrc=3044"
title="MP3">MP3</a>
and
24-bit
<a
href="/wiki/Free_Lossless_Audio_Codec?qsrc=3044"
title="Free
Lossless
Audio
Codec">FLAC</a>
format.
Although
their
output
has
come
to
include
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Anthology?qsrc=3044#Albums"
title="The
Beatles
Anthology">vault
items</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Love_(The_Beatles_album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Love
(The
Beatles
album)">remixed
mash-ups</a>,
the
core
Beatles
discography
recorded
during
the
1960s
is
217
songs
and
approximately
ten
hours
of
music.</p>








<p>Most
of
The
Beatles'
albums
were
released
in
both
<a
href="/wiki/Monaural?qsrc=3044"
title="Monaural">mono</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Stereophonic_sound?qsrc=3044"
title="Stereophonic
sound">stereo</a>.
Since
mono
record
players
were
the
most
common
at
the
time,
The
Beatles
and
their
regular
producer
<a
href="/wiki/George_Martin?qsrc=3044"
title="George
Martin">George
Martin</a>
gave
more
time
and
attention
to
preparing
mono
mixes
of
their
recordings.
The
Beatles
had
only
involved
themselves
in
creating
the
mono
mixes
for
the
first
four
albums;
the
stereo
mixes
were
prepared
without
their
supervision.
However,
because
by
the
late
1960s
stereo
record
players
became
more
common,
their
final
two
albums—<i><a
href="/wiki/Abbey_Road?qsrc=3044"
title="Abbey
Road">Abbey
Road</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Let_It_Be?qsrc=3044"
title="Let
It
Be">Let
It
Be</a></i>—were
mixed
and
released
in
stereo
only.</p>








<p>From
1968,
in
both
the
UK
and
the
US,
starting
with
the
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hey_Jude?qsrc=3044"
title="Hey
Jude">Hey
Jude</a>&quot;
and
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles
(album)">The
Beatles</a></i>
(better
known
as
the
&quot;<i>White
Album</i>&quot;),
new
releases
appeared
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Apple_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Apple
Records">Apple</a>
label.
<a
href="/wiki/Parlophone?qsrc=3044"
title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>
and
Capitol
catalogue
numbers
continued
to
be
used
for
contractual
reasons.</p>








<p>The
Beatles'
UK
discography
was
released
on
CD
in
the
late
1980s.
According
to
the
official
editions
of
the
first
four
albums,
they
were
released
in
mono.
The
remaining
albums
were
then
issued
in
stereo
only.
However,
the
sound
of
the
digital
transfers
of
the
discs,
produced
by
George
Martin
in
1987
and
1988
using
the
best
equipment
available
during
the
early
days
of
the
format,
no
longer
met
the
standards
achievable
of
21st
century
techniques.
From
2005,
over
a
four-year
period,
the
original
recordings
were
remastered
using
the
latest
technology.
Apple
and
<a
href="/wiki/EMI?qsrc=3044"
title="EMI">EMI</a>
released
these
versions
of
The
Beatles'
catalogue
on
CD
on
9
September
2009
in
mono
and
stereo.</p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Albums">Albums</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Studio_albums">Studio
albums</span></h3>








<p>The
following
table
includes
studio
albums
released
in
multiple
countries.
<i>Magical
Mystery
Tour</i>
was
released
as
a
six-song
double-EP
in
the
UK
and
as
a
longer
11-song
LP
in
the
US
(which
included
singles
and
B-sides
released
during
that
year).
When
The
Beatles'
catalogue
was
released
on
CD
in
the
1980s,
the
longer
US
version
was
chosen
for
release
and
is
now
considered
a
part
of
their
official
catalogue.</p>








<table
class="wikitable">









<tbody>









<tr>











<td>












<div
class="center"
style="width:auto;
margin-left:auto;
margin-right:auto;">












†











</div>
</td>











<td>Denotes
releases
that
are
part
of
the
core
catalogue:<br
/>
The
12
original
albums
as
released
in
their
native
UK
from
1962
to
1970<br
/>
and
the
US
<i><a
href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Magical
Mystery
Tour">Magical
Mystery
Tour</a></i>
LP.
The
<i><a
href="/wiki/Past_Masters?qsrc=3044"
title="Past
Masters">Past
Masters</a></i>
compilation<br
/>
is
also
included
as
part
of
the
core
catalogue.</td>










</tr>









</tbody>







</table>

<dt>









Studio
album
notes








</dt>








</dl>








<ul>









<li><b>A</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_a1"><b><a
href="#ref_note_a1">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_a2"><b><a
href="#ref_note_a2">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_a3"><b><a
href="#ref_note_a3">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_a4"><b><a
href="#ref_note_a4">^</a></b></span>
The
original
US
version
of
this
release
had
different
tracks
than
the
UK
version.
For
the
1987
re-release
on
CD,
the
US
track
list
matched
the
original
UK
track
list.</li>









<li><b>B</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_b1"><b><a
href="#ref_note_b1">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_b2"><b><a
href="#ref_note_b2">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_b3"><b><a
href="#ref_note_b3">^</a></b></span>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_b4"><b><a
href="#ref_note_b4">^</a></b></span>
US
sales
certifications
represent
the
total
sales
of
the
original
US
release
and
the
post-1987
version
with
the
revised
track
list.</li>









<li><b>C</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_c1"><b><a
href="#ref_note_c1">^</a></b></span>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Magical
Mystery
Tour">Magical
Mystery
Tour</a></i>,
released
by
Parlophone
on
19
November
1976,
was
the
official
UK
issue
of
the
US
album
which
originally
used
the
Capitol
masters,
which
had
<a
href="/wiki/Duophonic?qsrc=3044"
title="Duophonic">duophonic</a>
(&quot;fake
stereo&quot;)
mixes
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Penny_Lane?qsrc=3044"
title="Penny
Lane">Penny
Lane</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Baby,_You%27re_a_Rich_Man?qsrc=3044"
title="Baby,
You're
a
Rich
Man">Baby,
You're
a
Rich
Man</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/All_You_Need_Is_Love?qsrc=3044"
title="All
You
Need
Is
Love">All
You
Need
Is
Love</a>&quot;.
Its
re-release
in
1987,
which
coincided
with
its
release
on
compact
disc,
replaced
the
US
fake
stereo
mixes
with
German
mixes
originally
released
on
the
H&ouml;r
Zu!
label
in
1971.
It
became
part
of
the
official
catalogue
with
its
release
on
CD,
with
every
track
in
true
stereo,
on
21
September
1987.
As
a
US
import,
the
album
peaked
at
#31
in
1968.
Continued
sales
of
the
album
as
an
import
led
to
this
release.</li>









<li><b>D</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_note_d1"><b><a
href="#ref_note_d1">^</a></b></span>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Yellow
Submarine
(album)">Yellow
Submarine</a></i>
was
released
by
Parlophone
on
17
January
1969,
four
days
after
originally
being
released
by
Capitol
on
13
January
1969.
Also,
side
two
of
this
album,
which
is
completely
instrumental,
is
by
<a
href="/wiki/George_Martin?qsrc=3044"
title="George
Martin">George
Martin</a>.</li>








</ul>

<ul>









<li><b>A</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_compilation_a1"><b><a
href="#ref_compilation_a1">^</a></b></span>
The
1962
German
Polydor
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/My_Bonnie?qsrc=3044"
title="My
Bonnie">My
Bonnie</a></i>
was
credited
to
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan?qsrc=3044"
title="Tony
Sheridan">Tony
Sheridan</a>
and
the
Beat
Brothers&quot;.
All
subsequent
Polydor
albums
credited
the
band
as
&quot;The
Beatles
featuring
Tony
Sheridan&quot;.</li>









<li><b>B</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_compilation_b1"><b><a
href="#ref_compilation_b1">^</a></b></span>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Past_Masters?qsrc=3044"
title="Past
Masters">Past
Masters</a></i>,
which
includes
all
non-album
tracks
and
singles
not
released
on
any
of
the
12
original
UK
studio
albums
or
the
<i>Magical
Mystery
Tour</i>
album,
was
initially
released
as
two
separate
CDs
on
7
March
1988,
with
a
two-LP
vinyl
set
combining
both
volumes
following
on
24
October
1988
in
the
US
and
10
November
1988
in
the
UK.
The
original
CDs
were
included
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Box_Set?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles
Box
Set">The
Beatles
Box
Set</a></i>
released
on
15
November
1988.
A
two-CD
set
of
both
volumes
with
two
new
stereo
mixes
was
released
on
9
September
2009
as
part
of
The
Beatles
Remastered
project.
This
release
was
included
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Stereo_Box_Set?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles
Stereo
Box
Set">The
Beatles
Stereo
Box
Set</a></i>.</li>








</ul>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Extended_plays">Extended
plays</span></h2>








<p>The
following
Parlophone-only
released
UK
EPs
were
considered
official
at
the
time
of
their
release
and
were
re-issued
on
7
December
1981
on
vinyl
and
26
May
1992
on
CD
in
the
<i>EP
Collection</i>
boxed-sets
but
have
since
been
deleted
from
the
current
Beatles
catalogue.
All
of
the
songs
from
the
EPs
are
now
available
on
various
CD
releases.
Only
two
of
the
EPs
contained
songs
that
were
not
also
featured
on
their
albums
or
singles:
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Long_Tall_Sally_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
title="Long
Tall
Sally
(EP)">Long
Tall
Sally</a></i>
EP,
whose
tracks
can
now
be
found
on
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Past_Masters?qsrc=3044"
title="Past
Masters">Past
Masters</a></i>
CD,
and
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Magical
Mystery
Tour">Magical
Mystery
Tour</a></i>
EP,
whose
tracks
are
on
the
<i>Magical
Mystery
Tour</i>
CD
album.</p>

is
unknown</i></td>

</table>








<p>The
Parlophone-only
released
EPs
were
re-released
on
7
December
1981
as
part
of
a
15-disc
EP
boxed-set
called
<i>The
Beatles
EP
Collection</i>,
which
included
all
13
British
EPs,
both
mono
and
stereo
editions
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Magical
Mystery
Tour">Magical
Mystery
Tour</a></i>,
and
also
an
EP
of
four
stereo
mixes,
new
to
the
UK.
This
rarities
EP,
called
<i>The
Beatles
EP</i>,
contains
the
following
four
tracks:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Inner_Light_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Inner
Light
(song)">The
Inner
Light</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Baby,_You%27re_a_Rich_Man?qsrc=3044"
title="Baby,
You're
a
Rich
Man">Baby,
You're
a
Rich
Man</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/She%27s_a_Woman?qsrc=3044"
title="She's
a
Woman">She's
a
Woman</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Boy?qsrc=3044"
title="This
Boy">This
Boy</a>&quot;.
The
<i>EP
Collection</i>
was
re-released
on
26
May
1992
on
compact
disc.
<i>Magical
Mystery
Tour</i>
peak
chart
positions
were
originally
listed
in
the
singles
chart,
not
the
EP
chart.</p>

<ul>









<li><b>A</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_single_a1"><b><a
href="#ref_single_a1">^</a></b></span>
The
1962
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/My_Bonnie?qsrc=3044"
title="My
Bonnie">My
Bonnie</a>&quot;
was
credited
to
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan?qsrc=3044"
title="Tony
Sheridan">Tony
Sheridan</a>
and
the
Beat
Brothers&quot;.</li>









<li><b>B</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_single_b1"><b><a
href="#ref_single_b1">^</a></b></span>
Twist
and
Shout
entered
the
UK
Charts
for
the
first
time
in
November
2010,
on
download
sales
alone,
in
the
first
week
that
the
Beatles
back
catalogue
was
released
to
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.
It
peaked
at
position
48.
The
song
was
re-released
in
the
US
in
1986
and
peaked
at
position
23.</li>









<li><b>C</b>
<span
class="citation
wikicite"
id="endnote_single_cl"><b><a
href="#ref_single_cl">^</a></b></span>
Every
Beatles
single
which
charted
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>
from
1969-1986,
shared
at
least
one
week
on
the
chart
simultaneously
with
a
solo
single
by
one
of
the
four
Beatles.</li>








</ul>

<script
type="text/javascript">

(function()
{




$(document).ready(function(){
	
	
		$(".preview").click(function(e){	




		window.location
=
$(this).attr('value');	








});
		




	$(".preview").hover(function(e){	




		$('#preview').empty();




		$("#preview").append("<img
id='previewImg'
src='"+$(this).find('img').attr('src')+"'
alt='Smiley
face'
"+$(this).find('img').attr('value')+"='130'/>");	




		$("#preview")
				.css("display","block")




			.css("top",$(this).position().top
+
"px")




			.css("left",$(this).position().left
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","0")




			.fadeIn("fast");
			
			$("#previewAnc")
				.css("display","block")
				.css("top",($(this).position().top
-
1)
+
"px")




			.css("left",($(this).position().left
-
1)
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","1")




			.fadeIn("fast")
				.attr('onmousedown',
$(this).attr('onmousedown'))




			.attr('href',
$(this).attr('value'));








});
		
		$("#previewAnc").mouseout(function(){
			$('#preview')
				.css("display","none")
				.css("z-index","-1")
				.fadeIn("fast")
				.empty();
			$(this).css("display","none").css("z-index","-1");
		});
	
	});
})();

</script>

function
addEvent(obj,
evType,
fn)

{
	if(obj.addEventListener)

	{

		obj.addEventListener(evType,
fn,false);

		return
true;

	}

	else
if
(obj.attachEvent)

	{

		var
r
=
obj.attachEvent("on"+evType,
fn);

		return
r;

	}
	else
	{

		return
false;

	}

}
